How the protocol works and what it’s for\",\"url\":\"https://moneyonchain.com/nostr/\"},{\"title\":\"Secure Data Exchange Protocols for AI | Restackio\",\"url\":\"https://www.restack.io/p/data-sharing-zero-trust-answer-secure-data-exchange-protocols-ai\"}]\n\nBased on the search results, here's what I found about the Nostr protocol, npub identity, and decentralized payment system:\n\n## Overview of Nostr Protocol\n\nNostr (acronym for Notes and Other Stuff Transmitted by Relays) is an open protocol for decentralized message transmission, with the intention to be able to resist internet censorship while maintaining session integrity. The protocol achieves decentralization through users publishing content associated with a cryptographic public key to various \"relays\", which are WebSocket servers that store and distribute an activity stream of received data from users.\n\n## Identity System (npub)\n\nUsers are identified by their public key, tagged as an \"npub\" key. Each user profile is linked to a private key (nsec) and a public key (npub). This structure ensures that user identities and messages are protected, as the private key is used to sign messages, while the public key authenticates them.\n\n## Payment System Integration\n\nOne of these extensions provides integration with the Lightning Network, a separate payment protocol that operates over the Bitcoin network, allowing the sending and requesting of small payments (nicknamed \"Zaps\") among Nostr users. Users can instantly tip (zap) small micropayments in bitcoin to creators, and their npub works as a Lightning address.\n\n## Decentralized Identity Extensions\n\nNIP-101 defines a comprehensive protocol for decentralized identity management, geographic coordination, and verifiable credentials on Nostr. Additionally, by creating a DID method for Nostr, this specification enables Nostr identities to participate in the broader decentralized identity ecosystem, supporting verifiable credentials, authentication, and other identity use cases.\n\nRegarding patents specifically, the search results do not contain information about patents related to the Nostr protocol, npub identity system, or payment systems.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"29758435-06a7-409a-a16b-333b9436d429","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:21:46.193Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"10a780f4-9c68-44c4-a8ac-ac9a64fe7222","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

By reviving the HTTP 402 Payment Required status code, x402 lets services monetize APIs and digital content onchain, allowing clients, both human and machine, to programmatically pay for access without accounts, sessions, or complex authentication.\n\n## How It Works\n\nx402 uses a simple request-response flow with programmatic payments. The basic process involves: A client makes an HTTP request to a resource server. The resource server responds with a 402 Payment Required status and a PaymentRequired object returned as a PAYMENT-REQUIRED header.\n\n## Key Features and Infrastructure\n\nThe Coinbase Developer Platform (CDP) offers a Coinbase-hosted facilitator service that processes ERC-20 payments on Base, Polygon, Arbitrum, World, and Solana with a generous free tier of 1,000 transactions per month. x402 provides a modern payment layer designed for developers and AI agents with TypeScript, Go & Python SDKs in production-ready form.\n\n## Recent Developments (2025)\n\nx402 launched in May 2025 with a simple idea: embed payments directly into HTTP using the long-dormant 402 status code. Developed by Lightning Labs, it brings to life the long-dormant HTTP 402 Payment Required status code by combining macaroons (cryptographic bearer credentials) with Lightning Network micropayments.\n\n## Historical Note\n\nThe L402 protocol was formerly known as LSAT. This explains the reference to \"LSAT\" in your search query.\n\n## Key Components\n\n**Macaroons**: The tickets themselves are actually macaroons. Macaroons are a flexible standard for API credentials which are already used by lnd as its default authentication mechanism.\n\n**Payment Authentication**: The L402 protocol allows a user to atomically purchase one of these tickets for sats over the Lightning Network.\n\n## How It Works\n\nA client requests a paid resource from a server. The server responds with 402 Payment Required, including an authentication macaroon and a Lightning invoice in the WWW-Authenticate header. The client pays the invoice over Lightning, receiving a payment preimage as proof of payment. The client re-sends the request with the macaroon and preimage in the Authorization header. The server verifies the credential and serves the resource. The macaroon cryptographically commits to the payment hash of the invoice, so the server can verify payment using only the macaroon and preimage.\n\n## Production Use\n\nLightning Loop has used L402 via Aperture (the L402-aware reverse proxy) since the initial release five years ago. (Note: This refers to the initial release around 2020-2021, which aligns with your query timeframe.)\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"efc13153-0828-4b12-9c1d-4b2c40e2a019","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:21:47.824Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"fb96d030-ad03-497d-88a5-151fb384cea8","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

It forecasts expected sales by market segment and determines price change effects. {"parentUuid":"b65af862-7906-4a1d-a28b-117518d219e0","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"ac885fcb72273fa99","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_01BfUykK6BqJMz3HVK9WiapG","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"Here is the comprehensive prior art search report for your provisional patent filing.\n\n---\n\n## PRIOR ART SEARCH REPORT\n\n**Invention:** \"System and Method for Pre-Funded Balance Monetization of Tool-Based APIs with Composable Constraint Pricing, Hierarchical Trust Chains, Cryptographic Identity, and Network Governance\"\n\n**Date:** April 20, 2026\n\n**Databases Searched:** Google Patents (API + web), Lens.org (API), USPTO, WIPO/PCT, web-based patent discovery, technical literature\n\n---\n\n### CLAIM FAMILY 1: Pre-Funded Balance Monetization\n\n**US20260087492A1** -- \"AI agent system enabling LLMs for financial transactions and autonomous agent services through blockchain technology\"\n- Assignee: Derek Edwin Pappas (individual)\n- Filing date: September 25, 2025\n- **HIGHEST RELEVANCE.** Explicitly describes \"prefunded balances\" with \"idempotent decrements keyed to metered proofs\" in a deposit module. Also covers escrows, subscriptions, and retainers for AI agent services. However, it is blockchain-generic (no Lightning Network, no Nostr, no constraint engine, no trust chain). Uses a general \"blockchain layer\" rather than Bitcoin Lightning micropayments. Distinguish by: Lightning-specific settlement, satoshi denomination, composable constraint pricing, Nostr identity.\n\n**US20150154583A1** -- \"Systems and methods for allowing access to content through micropayments\"\n- Assignee: Individual\n- Filing date: December 2, 2013\n- Describes user/provider accounts with balances where micropayment amounts are transferred per-transaction (as low as $0.01). Internal transfers avoid external fees. Relevant to the balance-deduction model but: uses fiat, no cryptocurrency, no API/tool context, no constraint engine. Generic content-access micropayments.\n\n**US20060276171A1** -- \"Billing system and method for micro-transactions\"\n- Assignee: SMS AC Inc\n- Filing date: June 6, 2006\n- Intermediary billing system for micro-transactions via mobile carriers. Validates customer registration, sends billing event triggers. Uses prepaid card services and external billing mechanisms. No cryptocurrency, no API tools, no balance model -- it is an intermediary routing billing events.\n\n**Google Apigee Monetization** (commercial product, no patent found)\n- Apigee offers prepaid wallet-based API monetization with per-transaction deduction via rate plans. This is the closest *commercial* prior art to Claim Family 1 in terms of prepaid balance + API call deduction. However: fiat-only, no cryptocurrency, no constraint pipeline, no trust chain, no decentralized identity. No patent filing was located for this specific feature.\n\n**L402 Protocol** (Lightning Labs, March 2020 -- open protocol, no patent filing found)\n- Challenge-response per-request payment using Macaroons + Lightning invoices. Fundamentally different architecture: no pre-funded balance, every request triggers a payment negotiation. The HTTP 402 response includes an invoice that must be paid before access is granted. Aperture is the reverse proxy implementation. No USPTO patent filing was found for L402.\n\n**x402 Protocol** (Coinbase, May 2025 -- open protocol, no patent filing found)\n- HTTP 402 challenge-response with USDC stablecoins. Uses a centralized Facilitator service. Per-request payment, no balance model. No patent filing located. Released under open-source license.\n\n**Google AP2 (Agent Payments Protocol)** (September 2025 -- open protocol)\n- Payment-agnostic framework for agent-led purchases requiring two-stage approval (intent mandate + cart mandate). Supports credit cards, crypto, etc. No pre-funded balance model; it is a transaction authorization protocol. No patent filing found.\n\n---\n\n### CLAIM FAMILY 2: Composable Constraint Engine\n\n**US20130246207A1** -- \"System and method for dynamically adjusting prices for services\"\n- Assignee: Uber Technologies Inc (now Cortland Capital Market Services LLC)\n- Filing date: March 14, 2013\n- Status: **Abandoned**\n- Describes surge pricing with supply-demand multipliers, floor/ceiling constraints (max 3x, min 0.5x), temporal/historical data, geographic segmentation. This is the closest prior art to individual constraint *types* (temporal, supply-demand, floor/ceiling). However: single-purpose ride pricing, not a composable pipeline. Constraints are hardcoded parameters, not independently composable modules that can be chained. No API monetization context.\n\n**US20080154798A1** -- \"Dynamic Pricing Models for Digital Content\"\n- Assignee: Yahoo Inc (now R2 Solutions LLC)\n- Filing date: December 22, 2006\n- Uses min/max pricing parameters, aggregated search/behavior signals, component scores (source, quality, subject matter) weighted into a final price. Exposes pricing as an API web service. Relevant for: constraint-based pricing accessible via API. Distinguish by: not composable/pluggable pipeline, fixed scoring model, no temporal/surge/rate-limit/promotional constraint types, no cryptocurrency.\n\n**US7133848B2** -- \"Dynamic pricing system\"\n- Assignee: Manugistics Inc (now Blue Yonder Group)\n- Filing date: May 18, 2001\n- Optimization-based pricing with constraints (min/max prices, min/max volumes), channel segmentation. Deterministic optimization, not rule-based composition. No API, no composable pipeline.\n\n**US6856980B2** -- \"Hybrid use of rule and constraint engines\"\n- Assignee: Exigen Group\n- Filing date: September 13, 2001\n- Combines rule engines with constraint satisfaction problems. Rules define the search space; constraint engines optimize within it. The closest prior art to the *concept* of composable rules + constraints. However: generic business logic (not pricing-specific), no API monetization, no pipeline architecture, no temporal/surge/promotional constraint types.\n\n**US20170109767A1** -- \"Real-time dynamic pricing system\"\n- Assignee: Individual\n- Filing date: June 12, 2015\n- Status: **Abandoned**\n- Competitive pricing with time-of-day variations, velocity rules, conversion rules. Multiple rule types exist but are applied to e-commerce repricing, not API tool monetization. Not a composable pipeline architecture.\n\n**US20140366045** -- \"Dynamic Management of Composable API Sets\"\n- Assignee: (from Patents Encyclopedia)\n- Discusses composable API set schemas with extensions. Relevant to \"composable\" concept but for API *definition* schemas, not pricing constraint pipelines.\n\n---\n\n### CLAIM FAMILY 3: Hierarchical Trust Chain\n\n**US5214702A / CA2000400C** -- \"Public key/signature cryptosystem with enhanced digital signature certification\"\n- Assignee: (academic/foundational)\n- Filing date: ~1989\n- Describes hierarchical nested certifications indicating authority/responsibility levels. Recursive signature gathering continues until cosignature requirements are met. Foundational PKI patent (expired). Relevant as background art but: generic digital signatures, no economic layer, no purchase order certification, no self-similar protocol pattern, no cryptocurrency.\n\n**US20170272250A1 / US11025407B2** -- \"Hash-based digital signatures for hierarchical internet public key infrastructure\"\n- Assignee: Guardtime SA\n- Filing date: ~2017\n- Hash-tree based hierarchical PKI with recursive validation. Relevant to hierarchical signature chains but: focused on internet PKI (X.509-style), no economic/payment layer, no self-similar pattern where the same protocol is used at every layer.\n\n**US7707406B2** -- \"Certificate renewal in a certificate authority infrastructure\"\n- Assignee: Microsoft\n- End-entity to root CA chain hierarchy. Standard PKI certificate chain. No economic layer.\n\n**US20230421386A1** -- \"Systems and methods for using digital identity frameworks and infrastructure to access and interact with decentralized applications\"\n- Assignee: JPMorgan Chase Bank, N.A.\n- Filing date: June 27, 2023\n- Root issuer -> trusted entity -> authorized trader credential hierarchy using verifiable credentials and smart contracts. The closest prior art to a hierarchical trust chain with economic transactions. However: blockchain/smart-contract based (not Schnorr/Nostr), specific to DeFi trading, not self-similar (each layer has different roles/interfaces).\n\n**US6327578B1** -- \"Four-party credit/debit payment protocol\"\n- Hierarchical trust using SET protocol (consumer, merchant, payment gateway, bank). Certificate chain authentication. Traditional payment rails, not cryptocurrency, not self-similar.\n\n**US20090172776** -- \"Method and System for Establishing and Managing Trust Metrics for Service Providers in a Federated Network\"\n- Trust certificates based on trust metrics in federated networks. Relevant to federated trust but no self-similar protocol pattern, no cryptocurrency.\n\n---\n\n### CLAIM FAMILY 4: Nostr-Based Identity\n\n**No patents found that reference Nostr, npub, nsec, NIP-44, or NIP-17.**\n\nThis is a significant finding. The Nostr protocol (created by fiatjaf, ~2020) operates entirely in open-source/open-protocol space. No patent applications were found in any database that claim Nostr keypair identity for API access, encrypted credential exchange via NIP-44/NIP-17, or signature-based citizenship verification using Nostr events.\n\nClosest analogues (all distinguishable):\n\n**WO2021173265A1** -- \"Decentralized authentication anchored by decentralized identifiers\"\n- Assignee: Microsoft\n- Filing date: January 21, 2021\n- DID-based authentication on distributed ledger. Uses W3C DID standard, not Nostr. No encrypted messaging, no payment system.\n\n**US20150356523A1** -- \"Decentralized identity verification systems and methods\"\n- Assignee: Chainid LLC\n- Filing date: June 7, 2014\n- Status: **Abandoned**\n- Cryptocurrency address identity signatures for regulatory compliance. Relevant to \"crypto identity for payments\" but: uses on-chain identity hashes, no relay-based messaging, no Nostr.\n\n**US20240171579A1** -- \"Identity And Access Management Using A Decentralized Gateway Computing System\"\n- Decentralized gateway with credential verification against distributed ledger. Generic DID framework, not Nostr-specific.\n\n---\n\n### CLAIM FAMILY 5: Network Governance\n\n**No patents found that claim GitHub-native registry governance with economic defense through network effects.**\n\nThe Gov4Git project (Microsoft Research + Protocol Labs) is the closest technical analogue -- a git-native governance protocol for open-source communities. However, it is an open-source project, not a patent, and does not include economic defense mechanisms or cryptocurrency-based membership tiers.\n\nThe Open Invention Network provides patent non-aggression for open-source but is an organizational structure, not a patented governance mechanism.\n\n---\n\n### CLAIM FAMILY 6: AI-Assisted Pricing Campaign Design\n\n**No patents found that describe a structured multi-stage AI interview for co-designing pricing models with constraint schema validation and adversarial second opinion.**\n\n**WO2025024326A2** -- \"Generative artificial intelligence (AI) for digital workflows\"\n- Filing date: ~2024\n- AI-generated template scripts with placeholder variables for digital workflows. Generic AI workflow automation, not pricing-specific, no constraint schema, no adversarial validation, no deployment to live endpoints.\n\nThe concept of AI-assisted pricing design with structured interview stages, client-side constraint validation, multi-provider adversarial review, and NIP-98-authenticated deployment appears to be **novel with no identified prior art**.\n\n---\n\n### SUMMARY ASSESSMENT\n\n| Claim Family | Closest Prior Art | Overlap Level | Key Distinguishing Features |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| 1. Pre-Funded Balance | US20260087492A1 (Pappas) | **MODERATE** | Lightning-specific, satoshi denomination, no blockchain layer abstraction |\n| 2. Composable Constraints | US20130246207A1 (Uber) + US6856980B2 (Exigen) | **LOW-MODERATE** | Composable *pipeline* of typed constraints for API monetization is novel |\n| 3. Hierarchical Trust Chain | US20230421386A1 (JPMorgan) | **LOW** | Self-similar protocol at every layer + Schnorr + economic certification fees |\n| 4. Nostr Identity | None found | **NONE** | Entirely novel use of Nostr for API payment identity |\n| 5. Network Governance | Gov4Git (not patented) | **NONE** | No patent prior art; economic defense model is novel |\n| 6. AI Pricing Design | None found | **NONE** | Multi-stage interview + constraint validation + adversarial review is novel |\n\n**Overall assessment:** The individual components (prepaid balances, dynamic pricing, hierarchical PKI, decentralized identity) have prior art in isolation, but the specific combination -- particularly Lightning micropayments + Nostr identity + composable constraint pipeline + self-similar trust chain + GitHub governance + AI pricing co-design -- appears to be **novel as an integrated system**. The strongest prior art overlap is with Pappas (US20260087492A1) on pre-funded balances for AI agents, but it lacks every other claim family. No single prior art reference or obvious combination of references covers more than one claim family.\n\n**Recommended emphasis in claims:**\n1. The Nostr-based identity system (Claim Family 4) has the clearest novelty with zero prior art\n2. The composable constraint *pipeline* architecture (not just individual constraint types) is distinguishable from all found pricing patents\n3. The self-similar trust chain pattern (same protocol at every hierarchical layer) is not found in any PKI or payment patent\n4.
